Ken Binmore, [3mPlaying for Real [0m(New York: Oxford University Press, 2007). This textbook on game theory is light on mathematics. 

Ken Binmore, [3mNatural Justice [0m(New York: Oxford University Press, 2005). Why game theory matters in ethics. 

Colin Camerer, [3mBehavioral Game Theory [0m(Princeton: Princeton University Press, 2003). Some aspects of game theory work well in the 
laboratory, and some donโt. This book surveys the evidence, and looks at possible psychological explanations of deviations from 
the theory. 

John Rawls, [3mA Theory of Justice [0m(Oxford: Oxford University Press, 1972). Rawls is often said to be the greatest moral philosopher 
of the 20th century. He refers to the maximin principle as the difference principle when proposing it as a rational substitute for 
maximizing average utility. 

John Maynard Smith, [3mEvolution and the Theory of Games [0m(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 1982). This beautiful book 
introduced game theory to biology. 

Barry Nalebuff and Avinash Dixit, [3mThinking Strategically [0m(New York: Norton, 1991). A book-club choice, it contains many examples 
of game theory in action, both in business and in everyday life. 

Sylvia Nasar, [3mA Beautiful Mind [0m(New York: Simon and Schuster, 1998). A best-selling biography of John Nash. 

Alvin Roth and John Kagel, [3mHandbook of Experimental Game Theory [0m(Princeton: Princeton University Press, 1995). The survey by John 
Ledyard documents the immense amount of data supporting the claim that experienced subjects seldom cooperate in the Prisonerโs 
Dilemma. 

John Von Neumann and Oskar Morgenstern, [3mThe Theory of Games and Economic Behavior [0m(Princeton: Princeton University Press, 1944). 
Not a best-seller. Their theory of utility appears in an appendix.
